GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - beta*exp(-Abs(x))*v - mu*(c1 - v**c2)*v
Candidate formulas: 64

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v*(1 - v²) - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Let me first expand the GT:
`-0.0589613*v³ - 0.332588*v + 0.332588*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

Combining v³ terms: `(0.332588 - 0.0589613)*v³ = 0.273627*v³`

So GT = `- 0.332588*v + 0.273627*v³ - 0.111444*v*exp(-|x|) + 0.385230*sin(t)`

The GT has these terms:
1. A linear term in v
2. A cubic term in v³
3. A term `v*exp(-|x|)`
4. A `sin(t)` term

**Key issue:** The GT contains `exp(-|x|)`, which equals `exp(-x)` for x>0 and `exp(x)` for x<0. This is **not** the same as `exp(c*x)` for any single constant c, since `exp(-|x|)` is not an exponential function of x.

Also, `cos(c2 + t)` with appropriate c2 can equal `sin(t)` (set c2 = π/2).

Now let me check candidates. Most candidates have the form:
`c0*v + c1*cos(c2 + t) + c3*v³ + c4*v*exp(c5*x) + ...`

The core issue is whether `v*exp(c5*x)` can match `v*exp(-|x|)`. Since `exp(-|x|)` is not `exp(c*x)` for any constant c (it's a V-shaped function in the exponent, not linear), **no single `v*exp(c*x)` term can match `v*exp(-|x|)`**.

Could two exponential terms help? For example, candidate 29 has `c4*v*exp(c5*x) + c6*v*log(c7*exp(c8*x) + 1)`. Note that `log(exp(c8*x) + 1)` is the softplus function, not equal to `|x|` for any parameter choice.

Could `exp(c5*x) + exp(c7*x)` match `exp(-|x|)`? No, because `exp(-|x|)` is not a sum of two exponentials — for x>0 it's `exp(-x)` and for x<0 it's `exp(x)`, but a sum like `a*exp(bx) + c*exp(dx)` doesn't have this piecewise behavior.

Let me check if any candidate avoids this issue by having a different structure for the x-dependence... Looking through all 64 candidates, they all use either `exp(c*x)`, `log(c*exp(c*x)+1)`, `x^c`, polynomial in x, `1/(c*x+c)^n`, `sqrt(c+x)`, etc. None of these can reproduce `exp(-|x|)`.

Wait — candidate 13 has `v*log(c7*exp(c8*x) + 1)`. For large negative x, `log(c7*exp(c8*x)+1) ≈ c7*exp(c8*x)` (if c8>0), and for large positive x, `≈ c8*x + log(c7)`. This is the softplus, not `exp(-|x|)`.

Could two exp terms work? `c4*v*exp(c5*x) + c6*v*exp(c7*x)` — this would need to equal `v*exp(-|x|)` for all x, which is impossible since `exp(-|x|)` has a kink at x=0 while sums of exponentials are smooth.

**None of the candidates can reproduce `exp(-|x|)`**, which is an essential part of the GT that cannot be approximated by any combination of smooth functions of x available in these candidates.

Therefore, no candidate can be made exactly equivalent to the GT for all values of x, t, v.
